<span class="MHRHead">Pros:<br>- Intel Xeon processor E3-1225 4 core w. Hyperthreading<br>- 5X SATA III Ports on M.B.<br>- 6X USB 3.0 Ports<br>- 2X Display Ports<br>- 4X DIMM slots supporting up to 32GB RAM<br>- 4X PCIe 2.0 slots + 1X PCI slot on M.B.<br>- Upgraded Intel P4600 Graphics on Xeon E3-1225 v3 CPU<br>- Onboard Realtec HD Audio Card supporting Surround Sound<br>- Remote Access with Intel 9000 chip.<br>- Hardware support for RAID<br>- Cables for 6X 15-pin SATA connections.<br>- Extra 3.5" Drive bay with Cooling Fan in 2nd. 5.25" Drive Bay.<br>- Half-Height CD/DVD O.D. 5.25" has 3.5" HDD bay included.<br>- 2X Case Cooling Fans, 1X CPU Cooling Fan, 1X 5.25" Drive Bay Cooling Fan - Lots of Cooling.<br><br>Cons:<br>- ONLY 5-SATA III ports on the MotherBoard. If they would have put on<br>  6-SATA III ports, You could keep the O.D. and install 4-HDD's/SSD's<br>  for a nice RAID + 1 OS drive.  There was a spot to put the SATA III<br>  port on the board, it would have just cost a little more.<br>- HDD Drive Caddy's are flimsy plastic.<br>- Only 2X 3.5" Drive Bays included. UPDATE - New Versions have Total of<br>  4 - 3.5" Drive Bays.<br>- Only 1X SATA III Connector Cable included with box - Not enough for the 2 Drive Bays.<br><br>I have set up several of the i3-4130 version 70A4000HUX model of these TS140 servers so I already had the setup procedure and driver package ready to go. I have since purchase more of the 70A4001LUX with Xeon processors.  These are the best value for the money when they go on sale. I set up this box with the following in a couple hours:<br>- 12GB (3X4GB modules) pc3-12800 ddr3-1600 ECC UDIMM's<br>- LG Blu-Ray/DVD/CD Reader/Writer O.D. replacing the Half Height O.D.</span><span class="a-declarative" data-action="columnbalancing-showfullreview" data-columnbalancing-showfullreview="{&quot;rest&quot;:&quot;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;http://www.amazon.com/LG-WH16NS40-Internal-Blu-ray-Rewriter/dp/B00E7B08MS/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&amp;qid=1416945769&amp;sr=8-1&amp;keywords=LG+Blu-Ray+burner&amp;pebp=1416945771864&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;- ICY Dock Duoswap 2.5\&quot;/3.5\&quot; dual drive bays in 2nd. 5.25\&quot; bay.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;http://www.amazon.com/DuoSwap-MB971SP-B-Drive-Caddy-Docking/dp/B007Q4EZEA/ref=sr_1_fkmr0_1?ie=UTF8&amp;qid=1416945705&amp;sr=8-1-fkmr0&amp;keywords=ICY+doc+duoswap&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;  UPDATE: It isn&#39;t really necessary to put in the ICY Dock Duoswap bay&lt;br /&gt;  unless you want to access the SSD/HDD from the front.  You can put&lt;br /&gt;  the SSD in a 2.5\&quot; to 3.5\&quot; caddy in back of the 3.5\&quot; bay.&lt;br /&gt;- Sabrent 75-in-1 Multi-Card reader/writer in 3.5\&quot; exterior bay.&lt;br /&gt;- 3X Seagate 4TB HDD&#39;s&lt;br /&gt;- Crucial M500 480GB SATA III SSD for O.S. and Programs&lt;br /&gt;- Intel i350-T2 Gigabit PCIe Dual Port Ethernet Adapter Card&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;http://www.amazon.com/Ethernet-Server-Adapter-I350-T2-Full-height/dp/B005ATA16Y/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&amp;qid=1416945840&amp;sr=8-1&amp;keywords=i350-t2&amp;pebp=1416945842463&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;- Hauppauge WinTV-HVR-2250 Dual TV Tuner PCIe Card&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;http://www.amazon.com/Hauppauge-WinTV-HVR-2250-WINTV-HVR-2250-C-CARD-Express/dp/B0071N06G2/ref=sr_1_6?ie=UTF8&amp;qid=1416945895&amp;sr=8-6&amp;keywords=Hauppauge+WinTV-HVR-2250+Dual+TV+Tuner+PCIe+Card&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;When using Windows 7 Pro 64-Bit OS I get the following WEI scores:&lt;br /&gt;Processor:  7.7&lt;br /&gt;Memory:  7.7&lt;br /&gt;Graphics:  6.7 (with the P4600 CPU Graphics)&lt;br /&gt;Gaming Graphics:  6.7&lt;br /&gt;Primary Hardisk:  7.9&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;cpubenchmark.net has information about the relative performance and cost of the CPU&#39;s.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;http://www.cpubenchmark.net/cpu_list.php&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Here are some processor benchmarks for comparison:&lt;br /&gt;AMD Turion II 2.2GHz  -Dual Core  -1405 score -(HP Proliant N54L)&lt;br /&gt;i5-2520M 2.5GHz  -Dual Core  -3549 score -(HP Elitebook 8460p Laptop PC)&lt;br /&gt;i3-4130 3.4GHz  -Dual Core  -4801 score&lt;br /&gt;Xeon E3-1225 v3 3.2GHz  -Quad Core  -6998 score&lt;br /&gt;i5-4570 3.2GHz  -Quad Core  -7073 score&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;http://www.cpubenchmark.net/compare.php?cmp[]=2015&amp;cmp[]=1993&amp;cmp[]=1896&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The cpumark score is important if you are trying to stream high quality videos.  According to plex.tv forums, a cpumark score of 1500, or higher, is needed to stream a single 720p video without hangups.  A cpumark score of 2000, or higher, is needed to stream a single 1080p video without hangups.  The i3-4130 can effectively stream 2 - 1080p videos simultaneously and the Xeon E3-1225v3 can effectively stream 3 - 1080p videos simultaneously without hangups. You would have to go to the i7-4770 CPU or the AMD FX-8350 CPU (will not work on the LGA 1150 M.B. of a Lenovo TS-140) to get better streaming capability.  The AMD Turion II processor in the HP Proliant N54L struggles to stream one 720p video.  I own one of those and have built others for clients.  They are a nice compact data server but, they are outdated and very difficult to upgrade.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I ran some Transcoding tests comparing the i3-4130 CPU to the Xeon E3-1225 v3 CPU version using the freeware program Handbrake to transcode ISO files into .m4v files. Using the same iso file and the same transcoding parameters, I got the following transcoding rates:&lt;br /&gt;AMD Turion II  - &amp;lt;1frames/second&lt;br /&gt;i5-2520M  -  9frames/second&lt;br /&gt;i3-4130  -  29frames/second&lt;br /&gt;E3-1225 v3  - 59frames/second&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Xeon with its quad core was twice as fast at transcoding as the dual core i3-4130. The HP Proliant Microserver N54L can take literally days to transcode a full length movie iso file.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This is a great setup for a Media Server, HTPC, DVR, Data Server, or moderate Gaming PC.  You would have to add in a high end Graphics card to make this perform any better for 3D graphics simulations or high end gaming but those take too much power for the 280 Watt power supply. There are PCIe 2.0 slots for the card if you need it.  I put in a Radeon Saphire 6450 card just to check out the performance and the Graphics &amp; Gaming Graphics scores dropped down to 4.9 on the WEI.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Power supply is only 280 watts so you would have to upgrade that in order to meet the demands of a high end Graphics Card.  Lenovo does have a 480 watt P.S. in their parts list but there appears to be some difficulty in getting that OEM P.S. from them.  Bigger P.S. are available many places.  The power supply in the TS-140 has custom pin out configurations so it would be somewhat difficult to swap out a aftermarket power supply.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;As an FYI - The M.B. slots are PCIe 3.0 and 2.0 (Depending on which slot you are accessing).  I had difficulty in using cards I previously used in these TS140 boxes.  None of the PCIe 1.0 cards worked in these boxes even though PCIe 2.0 is supposed to be backward compatible with PCIe 1.0.  If you are planning on putting a Hauppauge TV Tuner card in this box, be sure that it is a model 88061 to work.  The 88041 or 88021 do not work with PCIe 2.0.&lt;br /&gt;UPDATE: I do not recommend these Hauppauge internal tuners anymore.&lt;br /&gt;  Unless you already have one that works in a PCIe 2.0 slot (model&lt;br /&gt;  #88061) they are a lot of hassle.  It is much easier to install&lt;br /&gt;  an external network tuner like the SiliconDust HDHR-3US tuner in your&lt;br /&gt;  network and connect to the server through Ethernet rather than running&lt;br /&gt;  RJ-36 Coax cable to the card on the server.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;http://www.amazon.com/SiliconDust-HDHomeRun-Definition-Digital-HDHR3-US/dp/B004HO58SO/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&amp;qid=1416946169&amp;sr=8-1&amp;keywords=SiliconDust+HDHR-3US&amp;pebp=1416946205296&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Similarly, the Ethernet Adapter cards are also picky.  Lenovo only recommends the Intel i350-T2 or i350-T4 cards.  I tried a Intel PRO/1000 gigabit 4-port adapter card that was PCIe 1.0 and it would not even post the BIOS. Other reviewers have been able to make the PRO/1000 work in the TS-140 by loading the correct drivers. So far, none of the drivers I found worked for me. I tried a DELL i350-T4 and that one also failed. There is a procedure to jumper the card and erase the Firmware to allow that card to be used in the Lenovo TS-140.  Unless you are very hardware savvy and comfortable with this type of procedure, I recommend that you use only Intel Branded or Lenovo branded Ethernet Adapter Cards to avoid the hassles.  I have little experience in these TS140&#39;s with other card mfg. like SYBA.  I installed the following card and had some problems with Jumbo Frames (MTU9000 is not supported).  Depending on your application, this may, or may not, work. They are a LOT less expensive than the Intel Ethernet cards.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;http://www.amazon.com/Syba-Ethernet-PCI-express-Controller-SY-PEX24028/dp/B00965J4TS/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&amp;qid=1416946561&amp;sr=8-1&amp;keywords=syba+ethernet+adapter+card&amp;pebp=1416946564484&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you are planning on adding RAM, take into account the following parameters:&lt;br /&gt;- ECC is OK.  Buffering/Registered is NOT.  ECC + Buffered/Registered RAM will NOT work in these servers.  I tried a couple brands and they would not even post the BIOS.  Lenovo sends Hynix or Samsung ECC UDIMM&#39;s with the machines.&lt;br /&gt;- The TS140&#39;s BIOS is NOT adjustable for RAM frequency or CL.  If you install RAM that is outside std. parameters, it will default to something that is probably slower than you expect and you cannot change it.&lt;br /&gt;Example: Lenovo set parameters are A. PC3-12800 CL 11 Voltage 1.5 volts  or B. PC3-10600 CL 9 Voltage 1.5 volts&lt;br /&gt;If you put in RAM that is PC3-12800 DDR3-1600MHz CL 9, 1.5 volts, it will default to PC3-10600 DDR3-1333MHz which is slower... even though the RAM is higher performance than specified.&lt;br /&gt;- Non-ECC is OK.  Just do not buy Buffered/Registered RAM.&lt;br /&gt;- I have used Hynix, Samsung, Crucial, and G-Skill modules in the TS140 server with good success.&lt;br /&gt;- Crucial&#39;s ECC server memory modules are a decent price here at Amazon&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;http://www.amazon.com/Crucial-1600MT-PC3-12800-240-Pin-CT2KIT102472BD160B/dp/B008EMA5VU/ref=pd_cp_pc_3&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;- The Lenovo Forums for the TS-140 now indicate that there are Kingston&lt;br /&gt;  Memory kits that work.&lt;br /&gt;- SuperTalent has ECC UDIMMS that some people have stated work in the&lt;br /&gt;  Lenovo TS-140.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;http://www.ebay.com/itm/221327478531?_trksid=p2060778.m1438.l2649&amp;ssPageName=STRK%3AMEBIDX%3AIT&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you are interested in using these as real servers that run VM&#39;s on different platforms other than the Windows server family, there is a growing amount of information on sites like homeservershow.com or smallnetbuilder.com but the Lenovo website forum is still lacking.  Lenovo.com has a growing # of driver sets for many OS&#39;s.  Check there frequently for updates.  The installation CD&#39;s that come with the TS-140 have been updated.  The last date I saw on a server shipped in November 2014 was from May 2014.  The websites have drivers that are newer than that.  Lenovo does not send out notices of updates so you have to check for them yourself (HP sends out notices of what updates are available to registered users).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you are looking to build a modest server or high end HTPC, I think this is an excellent deal.  The features are better than the HP Proliant G7, G8, or even the 300 series servers and beat the heck out of the Lenovo PC offerings which are much higher priced.&quot;}"><a class="a-link-normal" Weiss</a>   </span> <span class="a-color-secondary"> on February 11, 2014</span></span></div><div id="revData-dpReviewsMostHelpfulAUI-R24GZ9U2U5Q3L5" class="a-row a-spacing-small"><span class="a-size-mini a-color-state a-text-bold">     Verified Purchase   </span>        <div class="a-section">   <span class="MHRHead">Great quality, and low price (at $399).  Frankly, I never thought a Xeon processor-based Windows server can be had for so little money. One could use it as a regular desktop by installing Windows 7 or Windows 8, and be plenty happy. This thing is so fast.  It could easily last 5-10 years without feeling the pressure of having become outdated.<br><br>BASICS<br><br>You must install at least the following:  a hard drive and an operating system. That's all you need to have this thing running for basic computing.<br><br>You may either install Windows Server OS to run it as a server, or desktop version as a home computer system.  An SSD is recommended for installing the operating system only, leaving room for a large hard drive as a data drive.<br><br>It comes with 4GB  memory installed. Additional 4GB-28GB memory is recommended, making the maximum 32GB. Because I intend to run virtual machines using the server, I maximized  the 32GB memory slots.<br><br>I installed a pair of 1TB disks configured in RAID as data drives (that's in addition to the small SSD with the operating system);  and another 1TB disk as a backup drive.<br><br>HARD DRIVE BAYS<br><br>Although it has only two 3.5" drive bays, two more (four in total) 3.5 drives may be installed into the 5.25" bays, one into the card reader bay, the other into the slim optical drive bay (along with the slim optical drive, instead of replacing it).  No adapter is needed, because the 5.25" bays have special holes for screws to mount the 3.5" drives directly.  Taking out and inserting back the 5.25" bays are as simple as pressing a metal spring.<br><br>There are enough power connectors for four hard drives, but you will need to provide your own SATA cables.  I think it came with only one SATA cable (perhaps two?</span><span class="a-declarative" data-action="columnbalancing-showfullreview" data-columnbalancing-showfullreview="{&quot;rest&quot;:&quot;  I don&#39;t remember).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;ETHERNET PORTS&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you need to run it as a server, especially if you wish to configure the server to run as a router (instead of using a separate NAT router), you may need a better multi-port ethernet adapter. Intel i350-T2 it is a good choice, or you may want to try the cheaper &lt;a class=\&quot;a-link-normal\&quot; href=\&quot;http://www.amazon.com/Intel-1000-Dual-Server-Adapter/dp/B000BMZHX2/ref=cm_cr_dp_asin_lnk/176-6565053-5517616\&quot;&gt;Intel  PRO/1000 Pt Dual Port Server Adapter&lt;/a&gt; ).  If you are getting the cheaper Intel PRO/1000 Pt Dual Port Server Adapter, carefully read some of the reviews of that product to figure out how to update the adapter using unsupported drivers for i350-T2, for otherwise you could have boot image failure issues. This is very important if you don&#39;t want to waste tons of time.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;But if they don&#39;t need it as a server, the computer does have a built-in Ethernet port, and would be good enough if used as a regular desktop computer.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;ISSUES EXPERIENCED:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;1.  Virtualization configuration:  the BIOS of the machine by default has the Intel virtualization technology disabled.  If you would like to run virtual machines (virtual desktops) on this machine, you will need to enable it in the BIOS.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;It took me quite a bit time to figure out what the problem was and how to fix it.  The startup screen passes the BIOS setup quickly without displaying a clue on how to enter into the BIOS menu.  Turned out it is the \&quot;F1\&quot; key (not the usual F2 or F8) that you need to press as soon as the computer displays the first image.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Besides, in the BIOS menu, it isn&#39;t obvious where the virtualization toggle is located. Again took me a while.  It turned out to be under \&quot;Advanced\&quot; &gt; \&quot;CPU setup\&quot;.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;2. Another issue I encountered is quite odd.  When I used the optical drive to install the operating system, the install failed with an error message saying that files are corrupted. But I knew that was not the case, because the same disc was used to successfully install the same operating system on other machines.  So I ended up creating a bootable USB flash drive to install the operating system instead of using a CD in the optical drive.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;But with a failed partial install already on the hard drive, things could become messy from that point. To ensure that computer would boot from the USB drive instead of going into the botched partial install of the Windows, the BIOS settings should be changed to specify a strict order of boot devices. Because I did not initially figure out how to enter into the BIOS settings, I ended up doing it the hard way. I took out the hard drive, connected it to another computer, completely reformatted the hard drive, and reconnected it back to the ThinkServer.  After that, the computer automatically boots to the bootable USB flash drive that contains the operating system.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;To avoid the above problem, I would suggest that you use a USB flash drive to install the operating system from the very beginning, giving no chance for the optical drive to mess up things.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I have used the optical drive for other purposes since then, and have not encountered any similar problems. So the optical drive itself seems fine.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;OTHER COMMENTS:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The computer is quiet.  One could build an even quieter custom PC using very special coolers and fans, but this server computer is doing fine with the seemingly ordinary parts, far quieter than an average consumer PC.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The power supply is weak, but as long as you don&#39;t plan to run a very power-consuming video card, it should be fine, even with multiple hard drives. I use a UPS as an external power supply, which, to a server, is necessary. So I don&#39;t need to be picky on the quality of the internal power supply.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall, the server computer is very well made.  Even the wiring is of satisfactory quality.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I honestly can&#39;t find any serious fault of this server computer, especially considering the price.&quot;}"><a class="a-link-normal" href="http://www.amazon.com/Lenovo-ThinkServer-70A4001LUX-E3-1225-Processor/product-reviews/B00FE29IWK/ref=cm_cr_dp_text/176-6565053-5517616?ie=UTF8&showViewpoints=0&sortBy=byRankDescending#R24GZ9U2U5Q3L5"><span Both boxes have 2-port NIC card Syba Dual LAN Ports (SD-PEX24033) installed, running Win 2012 & 2012 R2 servers with Hyper-V hosting  a few win2012 / 2008 servers & Win8.1pro. Both are configured with Raid 10 and 4 Hdds installed in each server using the existing hardware with add-on screws. (Initially I tried out with Raid5 configuration but the Raid driver performance was disappointing with constant high access rate on the hdds.) The Xeon server is used on production as a domain controller setup with DNS & WSUS roles as well as a DVR recording video streams from 10 IP cameras 24X7 over the home office LAN. Remote login is installed so it allows me to see the real time surveillance monitor display when I am away from home. The i3 server is used for training & development to upgrade my skills in servers and networking.  The Xeon is a 4-core with a better GPU so it handles video/graphic better than the i3 and noticeably overall performance increase of at least 15% than the i3 & maybe higher in other categories. These are very good servers due to their low cost, durability, easy expandability and good functionality including low power consumption and whisper quietness. </div>  </div>             <a It's been working very well - silently humming along, backing up my home network of PCs, serving videos, giving me remote access when I need it. I've been slowly increasing my demands on that box - running Plex to replace Windows Media Center, and running BlueIris to manage a handful of IP cameras brought it to it's knees. With a Passmark just under 700 (Athlon Turion) it was never really powerful enough to do more than serve files. Unfortunately, the CPU is soldered to the mainboard and there's no way to upgrade it.<br><br>I discovered this server from the reviews at WeGotServed and WindowsHomeServerShow. People really seemed to like it, and after doing some comparisons, I understood why.<br><br>First off - from a CPU performance standpoint, this can't be beat. With a Passmark of just under 7000, it's 10x more powerful than the current HP server, and actually just a bit more powerful than my quad-core i5 desktop computer. This machine has enough power for everything I want to do with it today - and a lot of headroom for what's next. And if I need more power, the CPU is upgrade-able.<br><br>Next, there's enough space inside to easily hold 4 hard (2 dedicated 3.5&#34; bays plus 2 5.25&#34; bays that accommodate 3.5&#34; drives). Adding 4 hard drives + the included slim optical does fill up all 5 available SATA connectors on the MoBo. It does look like you could possibly squeeze in another slim 3.5&#34; or 2.5&#34; SSD if you really wanted to, but you'd have to add another SATA board. Which is something you may want to consider doing - as there are no eSATA ports on the back. I suggest the StarTech PCI card that has 2 eSATA ports externally + 2 SATA ports internally.</span><span class="a-declarative" data-action="columnbalancing-showfullreview" data-columnbalancing-showfullreview="{&quot;rest&quot;:&quot;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;RAM- I took out the DDR from my HP box and put them into this box. WHS only supports 8Gb, so no advantage right now to putting any more than that in.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;And now for the best part ... I decided to be optimistically adventurous and move the 4 drives from my existing server ... to my utter amazement it booted. I used the Lenovo CD to update the drivers, and after doing a couple of license reactivations, I was fully operational in about an hour.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Over the last few days I&#39;ve been amazed at just how quiet this server is - about as quiet as the MicroServer. I think it will draw some more power vs the previous server, but hopefully not so much that it will be painful when I get the electric bill.&quot;}"><a class="a-link-normal" href="http://www.amazon.com/Lenovo-ThinkServer-70A4001LUX-E3-1225-Processor/product-reviews/B00FE29IWK/ref=cm_cr_dp_text/176-6565053-5517616?ie=UTF8&showViewpoints=0&sortBy=byRankDescending#R2DTHKMQ7O3V5X"><span
